<span id="freeTextContainer17243305824167138313">The Southland's funniest son chronicles the year he braved the North in a memoir that is sexy, utterly hilarious, and one hundred percent new material. Grizzard is a perennial New York Times bestselling author, and his newspaper column is now syndicated in more than 400 papers nationwide. His latest effort is certain to be another smash hit. TV profile on "60 Minutes".</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_149121257">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149121257" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1795451-susan" class="left imgcol" title="Susan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1268971346p2/1795451.jpg" alt="Susan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/149121257?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 07, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1795451-susan" class="user" title="Susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1820772.If_I_Ever_Get_Back_to_Georgia_I_m_Gonna_Nail_My_Feet_to_the_Ground" title="Hardcover 9780394587257" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer149121257">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12622817086222548096">In the late'80s and early '90s when my dad was reading and enjoying Lewis Grizzard, I was too young to read the books myself. After reading "If I Ever Get Back..." I can say that I too am a fan. <br /><br />The book is still funny despite the fact that the humor and references are a little dated. It provided an interesting look at how his career evolved, but it did drag a little in places, which is what kept me from giving it a full 5 star rating. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_7128819">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7128819" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/122606-chelsea" class="left imgcol" title="Chelsea"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1183949008p2/122606.jpg" alt="Chelsea" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/7128819?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 28, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/122606-chelsea" class="user" title="Chelsea">Chelsea</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/147434.If_I_Ever_Get_Back_to_Georgia_I_m_Gonna_Nail_My_Feet_to_the_Ground" title="Paperback 9780345419279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=memoir" class="actionLinkLite">memoir</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=booksandwords" class="actionLinkLite">booksandwords</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=sports" class="actionLinkLite">sports</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/122606-chelsea?shelf=2007" class="actionLinkLite">2007</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7128819">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12559147088445904646">A deliciously funny book, much in the way of <a title="Bill Bryson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Bill%20Bryson">Bill Bryson</a> or <a title="Calvin Trillin" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Calvin%20Trillin">Calvin Trillin</a>, and I've made my love for those to authors abundantly clear. Grizzard knows how to write, and he knows how to talk about writing, and the man is a born storyteller.<br /><br />I'm afraid to say that I missed out on some of the jokes, because I:<br />1. hail from the North<br />2. am only interested in baseball, and that narrow focus is a kind of blasphemy as far as sports writer Grizzard is concerned<br />3. read my news online more often than not<br />4.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12559147088445904646">A deliciously funny book, much in the way of <a title="Bill Bryson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Bill%20Bryson">Bill Bryson</a> or <a title="Calvin Trillin" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Calvin%20Trillin">Calvin Trillin</a>, and I've made my love for those to authors abundantly clear. Grizzard knows how to write, and he knows how to talk about writing, and the man is a born storyteller.<br /><br />I'm afraid to say that I missed out on some of the jokes, because I:<br />1. hail from the North<br />2. am only interested in baseball, and that narrow focus is a kind of blasphemy as far as sports writer Grizzard is concerned<br />3. read my news online more often than not<br />4. wasn't alive for the vast majority of the happenings discussed in the book, meaning that I have no idea who the majority of the people mentioned are, and don't get a lot of the pop culture references.<br /><br />That said, I loved the book. Did I mention the guy could tell a story? And he has the storyteller's talent of surround himself with talented, crazy people, all of whom are much-loved fodder for said stories. Every author should love their subject as much as Grizzard does.<br /><br />Seriously, it's a hoot.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/4877713-paul-pessolano" class="user" title="Paul Pessolano">Paul Pessolano</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/147434.If_I_Ever_Get_Back_to_Georgia_I_m_Gonna_Nail_My_Feet_to_the_Ground" title="Paperback 9780345419279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1359085911">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8664938094708546351">“If I Ever Get Back to Georgia, I’m Gonna Nail My Feet to the Ground”, by Lewis Grizzard published by Villard Books.<br /><br />Category – Humor Publication Date – October 01, 1990<br /><br />This is another Lewis Grizzard book that is full of humor but may well be classified as his autobiography (up to this time).<br /><br />The book tells of his early life as a Army brat, his parents divorce, and living in the small Georgia town of Moreland. It tells of his entrance into the University of Georgia and how he was hired to work the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8664938094708546351">“If I Ever Get Back to Georgia, I’m Gonna Nail My Feet to the Ground”, by Lewis Grizzard published by Villard Books.<br /><br />Category – Humor Publication Date – October 01, 1990<br /><br />This is another Lewis Grizzard book that is full of humor but may well be classified as his autobiography (up to this time).<br /><br />The book tells of his early life as a Army brat, his parents divorce, and living in the small Georgia town of Moreland. It tells of his entrance into the University of Georgia and how he was hired to work the football games and was hired by the Athens Daily News. He chronicles his graduation from college, and being hired by the Atlanta paper to cover sports. He always loved the newspaper business and found a home in Atlanta. He also tells of his love for the party life, his love of Southern food and drink. It is during this time that he married and divorced his first wife. He found great success and was offered a plum position to move to Chicago, a move he sorely regrets. Chicago saw his second marriage fail, a bout with racism, and cold, cold weather. He returns to Atlanta and finds his real calling was doing a humor column and the rest is history.<br /><br />What Grizzard likes about newspapers:<br /><br />They ain’t heavy, except on Sunday<br />The are brief about the weather, television weather lasts longer than some thunderstorms<br />The personal ads. They keep me up on what’s kinky<br />Newspapers make great starters for fireplaces<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8664938094708546351">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_137474772">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137474772" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3499025-khristina" class="left imgcol" title="Khristina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1269973658p2/3499025.jpg" alt="Khristina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/137474772?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 04, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3499025-khristina" class="user" title="Khristina">Khristina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/147434.If_I_Ever_Get_Back_to_Georgia_I_m_Gonna_Nail_My_Feet_to_the_Ground" title="Paperback 9780345419279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer137474772">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9457924392877755574">I am so excited to be reading this book! One day I asked Joe what influenced him to attend the University of Georgia and he shared that it was reading Lewis Grizzard books when he was growing up. So, for Christmas this year, be bought me his favorite Grizzard book (a biography vs a collection of columns like his other books) and I am eating it up. <br /><br />Some interesting points so far, pg. 116 - Grizzard introduces fellow co-worker - Larry Young - my Dad's name! He also talks a fair amount about the Co</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9457924392877755574">I am so excited to be reading this book! One day I asked Joe what influenced him to attend the University of Georgia and he shared that it was reading Lewis Grizzard books when he was growing up. So, for Christmas this year, be bought me his favorite Grizzard book (a biography vs a collection of columns like his other books) and I am eating it up. <br /><br />Some interesting points so far, pg. 116 - Grizzard introduces fellow co-worker - Larry Young - my Dad's name! He also talks a fair amount about the Columbus Ledger Enquirer which is my hometown newspaper and where I completed my Senior high school internship project ( I once was an aspiring journalist making Grizzard's story even more intriguing.) <br /><br />Pg 140 - Grizzard tells a story about his good friend and coworker Browny and how Browny falls in love with his wife after seeing a picture of her daughter. That's exactly the story my parents share about how they met! My uncle began working at the same firm as my Dad and had a picture of my sister on his desk. My then not Dad saw the picture and asked my uncle who the girl was. When my Mom came to visit my uncle at work later, he introduced my Mom as the girl in the pictures Mom. My Dad later called my Mom and asked her on a date. And the rest is history!<br /><br />Pg 143 - Grizzard had a Basset Hound named Plato. I have a Basset Hound named Willie Mae!<br /><br />Finally, I didn't realize that this book was going to talk so much about my new home town, Athens! I've enjoyed getting to know more about the newspapers and town back when Grizzard was a UGA student.<br /><br />Looking forward to continuing this read.<br /><br />I can't believe I only read one book all Winter Break. I must be slowing down big time! Need to pick up the pace in 2011. 2010 is going to be a hard year to follow with such reads as Lonesome Dove and Gone With the Wind covered.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9457924392877755574">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/189840-a?shelf=books-about-the-south" class="actionLinkLite">books-about-the-south</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/189840-a?shelf=books-about-books" class="actionLinkLite">books-about-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4237674">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2625314829554844976">Unironically and seriously: one of the greatest books on writing I've ever read. A history of Grizzard's newspaper career, there's more off-hand writing advice in the first fifteen pages of this book than in whole books that are just about writing, and also it contains my favorite story about Hank Aaron breaking Babe Ruth's home run record <em>ever</em>. It features an elephant. I feel that's all I need to say.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/372740814?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 19, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1916753-carolyn-in-sc-c234d" class="user" title="Carolyn (in SC) C234D">Carolyn (in SC) C234D</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/147434.If_I_Ever_Get_Back_to_Georgia_I_m_Gonna_Nail_My_Feet_to_the_Ground" title="Paperback 9780345419279" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1916753-carolyn-in-sc-c234d?shelf=a-real-treat" class="actionLinkLite">a-real-treat</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1916753-carolyn-in-sc-c234d?shelf=r-t-newspapers" class="actionLinkLite">r-t-newspapers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1916753-carolyn-in-sc-c234d?shelf=memoir-biography" class="actionLinkLite">memoir-biography</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1916753-carolyn-in-sc-c234d?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer372740814">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer175184053954208504">I enjoyed this funny, funny book. I like newspaper stories, and this was the writer's account of how he started out working for papers as a kid, and progressed up to sports editor, then city news editor in Atlanta. He was eventually hired away to Chicago, but he didn't care for life there, and returned south to do columns. A very funny writer. (I'm pretty sure I've read another of his books, but haven't come across it yet in my reading records.)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('758plN+LdDsy8tsqhbpHq9Jdy3umSwiT2QyYNwVnPViKSxZHLVlgwb4qr5H726EZm6oIYu+WTzmzBZ2lyfLLHQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bWtvH5LXsUVX0iQhAm12ekPbvTFzxrjRJ3Tu9qT+tf4Iv1DMYAWlv9sKUJp8DJDICix+KDob/3tNfetkaGtDuw==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

Dave Barry\'s&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText13179643072616150666\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;If you\'re not already acquainted--nay, infatuated--with the works of the man who the New York Times calls &amp;quot;the funniest man in America,&amp;quot; you can get cracking right now with this all-time favorite collection of Dave Barry\'s humor columns. Dave Barry\'s Bad Habits won\'t rot your teeth, cause your insurance premiums to go up, or make your kids go cross-eyed if they sit too close to it. It will, however, make you laugh so hard your middle actually moves (the best exercise, and possibly the only kind you\'ll be interested in after forty). Here, preserved for all time, are Barry\'s profoundest musings on such topics as how to get kids to stop smoking (eliminate tenth grade), what to do if your car is making loud noises (turn up the radio), and a solution to the battle of the sexes (let the men do housework, say, for the next six thousand years to even things up). Politics and culture are analyzed, criticized, scandalized, and energized by comedians with no agenda other than to create the laughter and shock that comes from recognition and truth.\n\nPerhaps the greatest collection of comic talents ever between two covers, ¡Satiristas! is a collaboration between Paul Provenza—comedy\'s insider inquisitor extraordinaire, director/co-creator of the film The Aristocrats, and star of Showtime\'s The Green Room with Paul Provenza—and Dan Dion, comedy\'s most celebrated portrait photographer. Together, this cross-section of subversive comic artists offers insight into what drives them and makes them tick, and what drives them crazy and ticks them off.\n\nPaul Provenza\'s casual, intimate, artist-to-artist interviews are intelligent, outrageous, controversial, and even downright sick—but no idea or opinion is censored, and the unabashed honesty that results is funny, thought-provoking and inspirational.\n\nThe intimate photographic portraits by Dan Dion, comedy\'s Richard Avedon, are art pieces that take us through the stand-up routine to the person underneath, making ¡Satiristas!     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/85317.Lewis_Grizzard">About Lewis Grizzard</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/85317.Lewis_Grizzard"><img alt="85317" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1303841755p2/85317.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer11359950369072853847">American writer and humorist, known for his Southern demeanor and commentary on the American South. Although he spent his early career as a newspaper sports writer and editor, becoming the sports editor of the Atlanta Journal at age 23, he is much better known for his humorous newspaper columns in the Atlanta Journal-Constitution. He was also a popular stand-up comedian &amp; lecturer.<br /><br />Grizzard als</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11359950369072853847">American writer and humorist, known for his Southern demeanor and commentary on the American South. Although he spent his early career as a newspaper sports writer and editor, becoming the sports editor of the Atlanta Journal at age 23, he is much better known for his humorous newspaper columns in the Atlanta Journal-Constitution. He was also a popular stand-up comedian &amp; lecturer.<br /><br />Grizzard also published a total of twenty-five books, including collections of his columns (e.g. Chili Dawgs Always Bark at Night), expanded versions of his stand-up comedy routines (I Haven't Understood Anything Since 1962), and the autobiographical If I Ever Get Back to Georgia, I'm Gonna Nail My Feet to the Ground. Although much of his comedy discussed the South and Grizzard’s personal and professional lives, it was also a commentary on issues prevalent throughout America, including relationships between men and women (e.g. If Love Were Oil, I'd Be About a Quart Low), politics, and health, especially heart health. <br /><br />He made us laugh and think at the same time. Indeed, during his lifetime, Lewis Grizzard heard himself described as "this generation's Mark Twain," "one of the foremost humorists in the country" and "a Faulkner for plain folks" by the national press. What he was, without a doubt, was a masterful storyteller, stand-up comedian, syndicated columnist and best selling author.<br /><br />Lewis Grizzard Museum: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://newnan.com/lg/" target="_blank">http://newnan.com/lg/</a><br /><br />New Georgia Encyclopedia entry:<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.georgiaencyclopedia.org/nge/Article.jsp?id=h-987" target="_blank">http://www.georgiaencyclopedia.org/ng...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11359950369072853847">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/85317.Lewis_Grizzard" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Lewis Grizzard...</a>
